data-carousel-item><article class="article-card article-card--two-column article-card--no-excerpt--sm-down" data-evt-val='{"control_fields": {"mparticle": {"keys": {"click_source_type": "click_source_type", "anchor_text": "anchor_text", "widget_title": "widget_title", "target_url": "target_url", "target_article_title": "target_article_title", "target_article_id": "target_article_id", "target_article_position": "target_article_position", "layout_section": "layout_section"}, "mp_event_type": "Navigation", "extra_keys": ["click_vertical_position_percentage", "click_vertical_position_pixels"]}}, "click_source_type": "widget-list", "anchor_text": "IESO completes first steps toward securing Pictou County generation capacity", "widget_title": "new-glasgow", "target_url": "https://www.saltwire.com/nova-scotia/new-glasgow/ieso-completes-first-steps-toward-securing-pictou-county-generation-capacity", "target_article_title": "IESO completes first steps toward securing Pictou County generation capacity", "target_article_id": "c7e73a92-4c5d-4156-9ec8-e4f05611ee3d", "target_article_position": "1", "layout_section": "new-glasgow-list"}' data-aqa=article-card data-article-id=c7e73a92-4c5d-4156-9ec8-e4f05611ee3d data-category-colour=default data-evt=click data-evt-typ=click data-tb-region-item><div class=article-card__content><div class=article-card__details><a aria-label="IESO completes first steps toward securing Pictou County generation capacity" class=article-card__link data-tb-link href=/nova-scotia/new-glasgow/ieso-completes-first-steps-toward-securing-pictou-county-generation-capacity> <h3 class="article-card__headline text-size--extra-large--sm-up" title="IESO completes first steps toward securing Pictou County generation capacity "><span class=article-card__headline-clamp data-tb-title>IESO completes first steps toward securing Pictou County generation capacity</span></h3> <p class=article-card__excerpt data-tb-description>PICTOU COUNTY – On Feb. 19, IESO Nova Scotia announced it had received conditional approval from the province’s Minister of Environment and Climate Change, Tim Halman, for an environmental assessment of its proposed fact-acting electricity generation project in Pictou County. “We are pleased to have our environmental assessment approved, and are actively reviewing all of the conditions included with it so we can get to work on fulfilling them,” said Johnny Johnston, president and chief executive officer for IESO Nova Scotia. “This is just one step of many still to come, as we work to secure critical new electricity generation capacity. Our proposal is essential to Nova Scotia’s ability to continue to meet growing electricity demand, transition away from coal, significantly reduce greenhouse gas emissions, and achieve Nova Scotia’s 80 per cent renewable energy goals — all in the most cost-effective way possible for Nova Scotians.” The provincial government’s conditional approval of the environmental assessment is not a final decision on whether the project will proceed. Rather, it enables Nova Scotia’s non-profit independent energy system operator to progress to the next stages of project development, including feasibility analysis, permitting, and environmental testing, while continuing engagement already underway with stakeholders. In addition to meeting the Minister’s conditions, IESO Nova Scotia needs to complete additional requirements, including: Securing several government-issued project permits Conducting rigorous environmental analysis and technical work, including aquifer testing Completing the Mi’kmaq Ecological Knowledge Study, currently underway Following the Impact Assessment Agency of Canada’s review process. IESO Nova Scotia has significant ongoing work to determine if one or both of the proposed sites, located in Marshdale and Salt Springs, are suitable to support the project. IESO Nova Scotia is conducting a comprehensive evaluation of both sites, considering environmental, technical, financial, cultural, and community impacts. “Public feedback is a critically important component of our evaluation of this project, and we will be continuing with the proactive Indigenous and community engagement we already have in progress,” added Johnston. “We began these engagements early last fall, just as our organization was being stood up. Our team will continue to meet regularly with interested individuals and organizations to share information, answer questions, and understand their many different perspectives. There are many opportunities still to come to have your voice heard.” IESO Nova Scotia is engaging a broad range of stakeholders, including First Nations leaders and Indigenous economic development organizations, local officials, and area residents, including members of the Community Liaison Committees for each proposed site. All of this work, from permitting and geotechnical testing to public engagement and economic analysis, will inform how IESO Nova Scotia moves forward on this project. Findings could impact decisions such as technologies used in the facility, operational strategies, site design and sequencing, and facility size. As part of this project, IESO Nova Scotia will conduct a competitive procurement process to select the proponent. The successful bidder will build, own, and operate the facility or facilities that will provide essential, on-demand power to support increased renewable resources on the grid and help keep electricity reliable for Nova Scotians at the best possible cost. Anyone looking to learn more about the proposed fast-acting generation project can visit the community engagement section of their website at www.ieso-ns.ca.</p> </a><div class=article-card__meta-bottom><span class=article-card__time> <span class=article-card__time-clamp data-tb-date> 19 hours ago </span> </span><span class=article-card__category> <a class=article-card__category-link data-tb-category-link href=/category/nova-scotia/new-glasgow/> <span data-evt-skip-click=true data-tb-category>New Glasgow</span> </a> </span></div></div><a aria-label="IESO completes first steps toward securing Pictou County generation capacity" class=article-card__image-link data-tb-link href=/nova-scotia/new-glasgow/ieso-completes-first-steps-toward-securing-pictou-county-generation-capacity tabindex=-1> <picture class=article-card__image><source data-srcset="https://smartcdn.gprod.postmedia.digital/saltwire/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/tk042310turbines6_291989277.jpg?quality=90&strip=all&w=344&type=webp&sig=loTJXpqFQ3PI0cjb_RsvTQ,
